     <p>
      <br/>
      This article presents a
      <b>
       list of
       <a href="/wiki/Military_occupation" title="Military occupation">
        military occupations
       </a>
      </b>
      . Only military occupations since the customary laws of belligerent military occupation were first clarified and supplemented by the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hague_Conventions_(1899_and_1907)" title="Hague Conventions (1899 and 1907)">
       Hague Convention of 1907
      </a>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hague_IV_1-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Hague_IV-1">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        1
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      are included In this article.
     </p>
     <p>
      <a href="/wiki/Military_occupation" title="Military occupation">
       Military occupation
      </a>
      is effective provisional control of a certain power over a territory which is not under the formal sovereignty of that entity, without the volition of the actual sovereign.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Prolonged_2-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Prolonged-2">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        2
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Benv_3-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Benv-3">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        3
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-The_case_of_Israel_4-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-The_case_of_Israel-4">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        4
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Military occupation is distinguished from
      <a href="/wiki/Annexation" title="Annexation">
       annexation
      </a>
      by its intended temporary nature (i.e. no claim for permanent sovereignty), by its military nature, and by citizenship rights of the controlling power not being conferred upon the subjugated population.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Benv_3-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-Benv-3">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        3
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Edelstien_5-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Edelstien-5">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        5
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6">
       <a href="#cite_note-6">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        6
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7">
       <a href="#cite_note-7">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        7
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      <br/>
     </p>
     <p>
     </p>

          </a>

        <span class="reference-text">
         In 2005, Israel disengaged its military forces from the Gaza Strip and no longer considers itself to be occupying the territory. However, in a
         <a class="external text" href="http://www.un.org/News/briefings/docs/2012/db120119.doc.htm" rel="nofollow">
          Spokesperson's Noon Briefing
         </a>
         " on 19 January 2012, Martin Nesirky, Spokesperson for the United Nations Secretary-General, stated "under resolutions adopted by both the Security Council and the General Assembly on the Middle East peace process, the Gaza Strip continues to be regarded as part of the Occupied Palestinian Territory. The United Nations will accordingly continue to refer to the Gaza Strip as part of the Occupied Palestinian Territory until such time as either the General Assembly or the Security Council take a different view."
        </span>

       <li id="cite_note-6">
        <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
         <b>
          <a href="#cite_ref-6">
           ^
          </a>
         </b>
        </span>
        <span class="reference-text">
         <span class="citation book">
          Phillipson, Coleman (1916).
          <a class="external text" href="https://books.google.co.uk/books?id=-z5HRoVEt90C&amp;pg=PA10#v=onepage&amp;q&amp;f=false" rel="nofollow">
           <i>
            Termination of War and Treaties of Peace
           </i>
          </a>
          . The Lawbook Exchange. p.10.
          <a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number" title="International Standard Book Number">
           ISBN
          </a>
          <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/9781584778608" title="Special:BookSources/9781584778608">
           9781584778608
          </a>

          <q>
           The difference between effective military occupation (or conquest) and annexation involves a profound difference in the rights conferred by each
          </q>
         </span>
         <span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AList+of+military+occupations&amp;rft.aufirst=Coleman&amp;rft.aulast=Phillipson&amp;rft.au=Phillipson%2C+Coleman&amp;rft.btitle=Termination+of+War+and+Treaties+of+Peace&amp;rft.date=1916&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.co.uk%2Fbooks%3Fid%3D-z5HRoVEt90C%26pg%3DPA10%23v%3Donepage%26q%26f%3Dfalse&amp;rft.isbn=9781584778608&amp;rft.pages=10&amp;rft.pub=The+Lawbook+Exchange&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook">
          <span style="display:none;">
          </span>
         </span>
        </span>
       </li>
       <li id="cite_note-7">
        <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
         <b>
          <a href="#cite_ref-7">
           ^
          </a>
         </b>
        </span>
        <span class="reference-text">
         <span class="citation book">
          Stirk, Peter (2009).
          <a class="external text" href="https://books.google.co.uk/books?id=4951aoUL5nEC&amp;pg=PA44#v=onepage&amp;q&amp;f=false" rel="nofollow">
           <i>
            The Politics of Military Occupation
           </i>
          </a>
          . Edinburgh University Press. p.44.
          <a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number" title="International Standard Book Number">
           ISBN
          </a>
          <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/9780748636716" title="Special:BookSources/9780748636716">
           9780748636716
          </a>
          .
          <q>
           The significance of the temporary nature of military occupation is that it brings about no change of allegiance. Military government remains an alien government whether of short or long duration, though prolonged occupation may encourage the occupying power to change military occupation into something else, namely annexation
          </q>
         </span>
         <span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AList+of+military+occupations&amp;rft.aufirst=Peter&amp;rft.aulast=Stirk&amp;rft.au=Stirk%2C+Peter&amp;rft.btitle=The+Politics+of+Military+Occupation&amp;rft.date=2009&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.co.uk%2Fbooks%3Fid%3D4951aoUL5nEC%26pg%3DPA44%23v%3Donepage%26q%26f%3Dfalse&amp;rft.isbn=9780748636716&amp;rft.pages=44&amp;rft.pub=Edinburgh+University+Press&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook">
